# PROBABILISTIC SEARCH ENGINE
COMP 479 / Fall 2016
Project 2
Jeremy Brown -- ID 27515421


## Application description

This application takes the basic SPIMI indexer & query system from Project 1 and aguments it with ranking.
Instead of using the boolean approach (AND/OR queries, all or nothing), this application instead takes
each document containing at least one word from the query and gives it a score. This score is calculated using the
Okai BM25 model. The query client then returns the results in order from the highest ranking score to the lowest.
This presents users with the most 'relevant' results first and the least relevant results last.

** Stopword removal is done by default to cut down on irrelevant results and the time required to run a query since
the presence of any stopwords in the query greatly increases the lookup time, and there is little usefulness in
including them in the search.


## How to run

### Building the dictionary
The script checks if the corpus is present in a predetermined location. If the corpus is not found, it will be
downloaded and extracted prior to continuing. If the --download-corpus flag is specified, the corpus will be
re-downloaded even if it was found. The script then parses, inverts, and merges the dictionary as seen in Project 1.

### Querying the dictionary
The querying is similar to Project 1, except that there is no longer a distinction for AND / OR queries. Instead,
any query is treated as an OR query, but the results are ranked in order of relevance. So for a three-word query,
any document with at least one of the three keywords (excluding stopwords) will be included in the results, but
documents with all three keywords and multiple occurences of the keywords will appear higher up in the list.


## What I have learned

I have learned that while the ranking algorithm employed here gives a decent idea of 'relevance' to the returned
documents, it is a rather simplistic model of relevance. It does not consider the order or placement of terms in
the document, therefore losing some information that can be important in determining the actual relevance of the
document. It does not include any consideration for phrase queries either, which also limits its ability to accurately
depict 'relevance' (i.e. it does not distinguish between 'Wheel of fortune' and '[...] ferris wheel. They had a quip
of bad fortune [...]'). These two algorithm considerations are important to reach a system capable of procuding
a 'relevance' level even approaching what we are accustomed to with the search engines we have now (Google, Yahoo,
etc.).
